< Text>
Nice little retreat.

Plenty of parking. Porta potties, sinks.

Trail has a lot of rocks, slight inclines, plenty of shade & a walking stick isn‚Äôt necessary (unless that‚Äôs how you hike). Plenty of pollen for allergies ü§ß. Majority of the hikers did not wear masks (I do though). Also a great spot for photography.<//Text>

<rate>5<//rate>< Text>
Amazing place. Must visit in Spring when the flowers are in bloom, and the water is flowing from the cliffs. Table mountain is a beautiful place where vintage California is on full display. Can be very crowded on weekends.< /Text>

It‚Äôs a gorgeous place if you are at the right time. You won‚Äôt get a chance to hike on a tabletop mountain everyday, specially when the wildflowers are at its peak. Trust me, its a spectacle. Only bummer is the crowd which can be overwhelming and distracting. Try to be early if you are planning to be on spring weekends.<//review>

<Review>Hiked to Phantom Falls with some friends on March 16th. The flowers were good, but had not peaked yet. Hike west from the parking lot for 0.4 miles, until you reach the old oak grove, and you will see the first trail sign.
We hiked to Hollow Falls also, and followed the trail posts to reach the pool at the bottom of the falls without having to scramble down a steep rocky slope.<//Review>< gmap_id>

<user_name>Holly Genevieve<//user_name><review>Trail was pretty easy. Definitely shorter than most that I have been on. When you use the directions on google maps make sure you find the directions that lead to the parking lot!!! I didn‚Äôt know that when I went and I got directions for phantom falls and it lead me to a different location! You have to make sure the location is on Cherokee road! The trail the whole time was very beautiful because of all the flowers in bloom right now and I would suggest going before they die or it might not be as nice. The waterfall isn‚Äôt super intense but it was still a very beautiful view and my friend and I even hiked to the bottom. If you do go to the bottom, do not bring dogs because people did and the dogs had a really hard time because the way to get there is really rocky.! There is a cave behind the waterfall so if you do bring a dog then be careful that they don‚Äôt go in the cave and fall. Overall, if you‚Äôre not going down to the bottom of the waterfall it‚Äôs only 6.5 miles and pretty easy. The views are amazing and getting to the bottom of worth it but be cautious and take your time getting down !< /review>< date>

< Text>
Phantom Falls is one of the most unique waterfalls I‚Äôve been to in CA.
Don‚Äôt forget to pay for a lands pass online.($5).
When I arrived at the trailhead,
I found out there was no trail at all.
I needed GPS and the All Trail App to help me and my cousin.
It is flat with rolling green hills and some wildflowers.( very pretty,amazing).
We followed an old fence and crossed over the fence.
There are 2 ways to get Phantom falls.
They are both the same distance and incredible view.
Getting down to the swimming pool of Phantom Falls was big adventure for us but it worth it.( we were using rope).
The view around Phantom Falls were spectacular.(you have to go down to the pool if you are here).
Some parts of the trail are muddy with a lot of small water  crossing.( hiking shoes with water roof is the best).
We were able to visit 4 waterfalls on our trip.
We didn‚Äôt have much water flowing but enjoy Landcape and wildflowers.
We will try to come back here again for wildflowers and the falls after few rains or sometime in early April.
(2/16/2020).</Text>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Beautiful, moderate 5 mile round trip hike to Ravine and Phantom Falls. There is no designated trail but you can see make where the trail has been formed by other hikers. At one point, you can take the left fork to see a smaller  waterfall. But if you continue right to the fork you will see Ravine and Phantom. Beware of private property signs! Once you reach tall grass, there will be a sign that points you in the right direction. No spring flowers unfortunately but we went on a rainy day and had the trail all to ourselves.< /Review>

< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< review>
A very unique waterfalls that flows over the edge of a shear cliff and into a valley about a hundred feet below. I did not hike down into the valley to the base of Phantom falls since the trail was difficult to find and rather steep, also since the water flow was minimal when I went to the falls. The round trip to the overlook of the falls from the parking area is about 4 miles and well worth it. Best to go in spring after a rainfall to see the vibrant wildflowers in bloom and the falls with more flowing water.<//review>

<Date>1555216857320<//Date><gmapID>0x809ccb8d3a5aa2ab:0x22891c478cf32162</gmapID>< review>
The hike to phantom falls is beautiful in April! It's a few miles hike, so bring water and some snacks l, maybe even a picnic. Some people brought kites. Make sure you stay to the right at the fork in the hike to make it to the 'big' phantom falls. Also, all these pictures of the falls are posted from a rocky cliff. It's a straight drop down and I'm not gonna lie it scared me with my kids.
Tips for directions to the parking spot: on maps type in Cherokee Road, Oroville. Theres a fork in the road so make sure you stay LEFT on Cherokee Road. You will see some random parking spots but if you keep driving you will see port-o-potties on the side of the road and you will know your at the right spot.</review>

<Text>We went to Phantom Falls in April 2018 shortly after the rains so that there was plenty of water running. We wound our way down into the canyon and enjoy the falls from the bottom as well. It was quite incredible! So very very beautiful and impressive! I haven't been here at any other time of the year but this year in April the flowers were gorgeous, small creeks running everywhere and worth every moment. We fell in love with it and came back for four weekends out of 5 so is to explore Phantom Falls Hollow Falls and the falls right there in the middle between the two. Exceptional, gorgeous. < text>
Just a peaceful area to enjoyed life. With friends, family or your love partner. You can choose from many types of hikes that suites your ability. You can visit all 3 falls if you have time. Once you get closed to the falls.

BEWARE!!! They are called Falls for a reason. People have gotten hurt and even paid the ultimate price. Don't let that discouraged you, the sites are worth seeing. Just be careful of your surroundings.

On your trip you'll see California Poppy and many wild flowers. BEWARE of the cow pies too. Hiking boots are a must if you want to wander and explored.

At this time of year of the wild flowers are blooming profusely. The waterfall itself, only flows during the winter and spring. The hike to the waterfalls is fairly easy. Just as the Table Mountain Reserve that contains Phantom Falls deserves five stars, the falls themselves also deserve a solid five stars. The setting is amazing, the falls are extremely impressive. On the right day, you'll even get rainbows showing in the falls.

One can also hike down to the base of the falls, and hike behind them. There is even a historic mine shaft behind the falls that one can view.

This is an amazing destination in Spring.<//Text>

102549337404707035983</UserId.>
< name>
Ryan Bavetta<//name>
<Time>1396334658618</Time>< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< review>
This is a spectacular hike during a narrow window of time each year. You need to go when the wildflowers are at their peak in the spring (the timing differs each year, check for wildflower reports online) and a couple days after it rains so that there is water in the falls. We did a loop to Phantom Falls then to Ravine Falls at the end of March. There was no trail to Phantom Falls, and there were so many wildflowers that in order to hike anywhere you needed to crush the beautiful flowers under you feet :-\ There was a route on the far side of Phantom Falls to the bottom of the falls where we checked out the cave formation and the Coastal Range newts swimming in the pool below. Make sure to bring a map as there will likely be no discernible trail to Phantom Falls. The parking lot can be found at these coordinates: 39.595923, -121.541736</review>

< text>
Got the savory waffle and the s'mores waffle. We got the smoked turkey and the guda on the savory waffle, it was very good. The savory reminded me of a grilled cheese, but there was small bits of carmalized sugar on the bottom side of the waffle. The added sugar was a nice little bit of sweetness, which if you are looking for just a savory taste may not have been the best option. The s'mores waffle had speculoos, dark chocolate and marshmallow cream. The combination did a great number of recreating the s'mores flavor and experience. There was a small bit of burnt marshmallow that just added to the campfire taste.<//text>

<review>"VOTED BEST WAFFLE IN AMERICA"?!
I don't think so.
Let's start with the good....our server even though a little slow was friendly and I could tell she was doing her best. It was the food that really disappointed me...actually to a degree where I felt almost ripped off. Here's why: When you go to a waffle place that specialized in waffles...you expect their waffles to be fresh! We waited close to 25 min, but I figured if it's fresh then it's worth the wait. The waffle was very stale, old and crunchy....like it had been sitting out the day before and they just refrigerated it over night and served the next day. Toppings are additional cost..which to be honest, is a bit surprising...considering most people expect something on their waffle (and this place is not cheap).
The Poached Eggs Plate was equally disappointing. I almost let out a chuckle when it got served. I've had better eggs and sausage at McDonald's - no seriously! The sausage was hard and too greasy and the eggs were your average tasteless...low quality with no seasoning eggs...if you're going to put paprika on eggs...sprinkle at least a little salt.
Voted Best Waffle...No! and unfortunately I won't go back even for ...well...anything.
You don't charge prices like this...where everything is additional like it's a steakhouse...and then serve your customers that degree of quality. :(<//review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPkuLxj0UN7ztgCmrBE-kIT-rXyaOMkExQZKArr=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPAo6vZ8DySBBnmJ0easebjoY7-Bv4wAPOjvgZT=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOU5M3r03BGaSdSOhVrAtxi-px_WF9c9jcIATO4=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOfXmLKgfDCiASKRYlonFsIaRPHCXguZwaNCNQK=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO6Rb-13_j67UjQmuX02uOLdSuGKynctUwFBAWv=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMidPRh2Bj4KZH5ghwQT8qbH58P4lty0uQWgrc6=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMLkrP0NnIQlUSyUYMOg14ku-Effn3YRIExU1do=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics>< resp>

<rate>3</rate>< review>
They say they won a prize for best waffle in the usa. Doubt it. The belgian waffles here are a bit off. You feel sugar grains in the waffles. Don't like that. Not sure they have the recipe right. Still this is the best belgian waffle I know about in Los Angeles.

Everywhere else shops commit the serious crime of selling you "upscale" eggo waffles or worse as "belgian". Yes, belgium came up with waffles but to he called belgian they need to at least try to make them authentic not just call them that. Belgian waffles are not sponges. They are relatively dense and rich. Some of the waffles out there are as belgian, as taco bell tacos are Mexican.</review>

<review>Really chill environment. Wasn't crowded and the vibe is very cozy and relaxing. David was very welcoming and helpful. I suppose it's easy to become apathetic about your job after a while, but he greeted me with enthusiasm and explained the menu very well - including letting me sample the speculoos and explaining what cold brew coffee was and that their waffles are made with a dough instead of batter. His recommendations were excellent and I enjoyed my waffle and Mocha Latte (which I appreciated for it's more subtle chocolate approach).

There's lots of seating and it seems laptop friendly. This would be a great place to get some work down. My only disappointment is with the operating hours - I feel that they close a little too early for my schedule, which means I won't get to be here as often as I'd like, but I also realize my expectations might be really high. Coming from NYC, I love late night culture. Guess I'll have to stick to Crave Cafe for my midnight oil.

Overall, this place was really neat, menu was easy enough to understand and I feel you really get that eclectic cafe vibe from here.</review>< gmap_id>

I moved in with my sister recently and was worried that there might not be a good sushi place nearby by. I love sushi, and have been to a good share of good and bad restaurants. I'm glad to say I am satisfied with Tokyo place. The waitress was friendly, and the sushi was good (we tried 3 different rolls).
